كتاب الرهن / تعريفه وشروطه وما يصح به والتصرف فيه
ومَن شرى شيئاً على أن يرهن شيئاً ، أو يعطي كفيلا بعينهما من ثمنه وأبي صح استحسانا
(ومن شرى شيئاً على أن يرهن شيئاً، أو يعطي كفيلاً بعينهما من ثمنه وأبى(۱) صح استحساناً، والقياس أن لا يجوز؛ لأنه صفقة في صفقة، وجه الاستحسان : أنه شرط ملائم ؛ لأنّ الكفالة والرهن للاستيثاق،
[١]
والاستيثاق ملائم للوجوب ، فاعتبار وضعه لهذا المعنى يوجب إرادته خاصة به غیره، فاعتبار وضعه لهذا المعنى يوجب إرادته خاصة، واعتبار وضعه لذلك المعنى يوجب إرادته خاصة فيلزم أن تكون كل منهما مراداً، وغير مراد، فلا يكون ذلك إلا بأن يراد أحد المعنيين على أنه نفس الموضوع له، والآخر على أنه يناسبه، فيكون جمعاً بين الحقيقة والمجاز، وهو باطل.
(
(۲)
وقال الشافعي له : يجوز ذلك بشرط أن لا يكون بينهما مضادّة، فإذا كان بينهما مضادة لا يجوز بالاتفاق، وكذا لا يجوز إرادة المجموع من حيث هو مجموع بالاتفاق ، وزيادة التوضيح في «التلويح» (٢). [١] قوله : ملائم للوجوب ؛ فإذا كان الرهن معيّناً والكفيل حاضراً في المجلس اعتبرنا فيه معنى الشرط، وهو ملائم، فصح العقد، وإذا لم يكن الرهن ولا الكفيل معيناً، أو كان الكفيل غائباً حتى افترقا لم يبق معنى الكفالة، والرهن للجهالة، فبقي الاعتبار لعينه فيفسد ، ولو كان غائباً فحضر في المجلس، وقبل : صح. ولو امتنع المشتري عن تسليم الرهن لم يجبر عليه، وقال زفر ه: يجبر؛ لأنَّ الرهن إذا شرط في البيع صارَ حقاً من حقوقه كالوكالة المشروطة في الرهن، فيلزمه بلزومه، ونحن نقول : الرهن عقد تبرع من جانب الراهن على ما بيناه ، ولا جبر على التبرعات.
ولكن البائع بالخيار إن شاء رضي بترك الرهن، وإن شاء فسخ البيع ؛ لأنه وصف مرغوب فيه، وما رضي إلا به، فيتخيرُ بفواته إلا أن يدفع المشتري الثمن حالاً لحصول
Book of Pledge: Its definition, conditions, what is valid, and disposal of it. And whoever buys something on the condition that he will give a pledge or give a guarantor, specifying both from its price, and then refuses [to do so], it is valid by istihsan. The qiyas is that it is not permissible because it is one transaction within another transaction. The basis of istihsan is that it is a suitable condition because guarantee and pledge are for securing, and securing is suitable for obligation. So consideration of its placement for this meaning necessitates that it is intended specifically. And consideration of its placement for that meaning necessitates that it is intended specifically, so it is necessary that each of them is intended and not intended. That cannot be except by one meaning being intended as the very thing placed for it, and the other as what is suitable to it, which is a combination of literal and metaphorical, and that is invalid. And al-Shafi'i said: It is permissible on condition that there is no contradiction between them; if there is contradiction, it is not permissible by agreement. Likewise, intending the totality as a totality is not permissible by agreement. Further clarification is in 'al-Talwih'. [1] His saying: 'Suitable for obligation': So if the pledge is specified and the guarantor is present in the session, we consider the meaning of the condition in it, and it is suitable, so the contract is valid. If neither the pledge nor the guarantor is specified, or if the guarantor is absent until they separate, the meaning of guaranty does not remain, and the pledge is due to ignorance, so the consideration remains for its literal [contract], and it becomes invalid. If the guarantor is absent but then attends in the session and accepts, it is valid. If the buyer refuses to deliver the pledge, he is not compelled to do so. Zufar said: He is compelled because when the pledge is stipulated in the sale, it becomes one of its rights like the agency stipulated in the pledge, so it becomes binding by its binding. But we say: The pledge is a gratuitous contract from the side of the pledgor, as we have explained, and there is no compulsion in gratuitous acts. However, the seller has an option: if he wishes, he may agree to forego the pledge, and if he wishes, he may rescind the sale, because it is a desirable attribute, and he only agreed to it, so he has a choice due to its loss, unless the buyer pays the price immediately to secure.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Pledge discusses the ruling on a sale where the buyer agrees to give a specific pledge (rahn) or guarantor (kafil) as part of the price, but then refuses to do so. The ruling is that the sale is valid by istihsan, although qiyas would render it invalid as it resembles 'one transaction within another' (safqah fi safqah). The justification for istihsan is that the condition of providing a pledge or guarantor is suitable (mula'im) for the contract because it serves to secure the obligation, and securing is harmonious with obligation. The passage then addresses a dispute with al-Shafi'i, who permits it conditionally as long as there is no contradiction between the condition and the contract. The text further details conditions for validity: the pledge must be specified and the guarantor must be present in the session; otherwise, the contract may be invalid. A second dispute is with Zufar regarding whether the buyer can be compelled to deliver the pledge; the Hanafi position is that he cannot be compelled because a pledge is a gratuitous contract, but the seller has the option to rescind the sale if the pledge is not delivered, unless the buyer pays the price immediately.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A pledge; property given by a debtor to a creditor as security for a debt.
كفيل (kafil): A guarantor; a person who takes on responsibility for another's debt.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that overrides qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling.
صفقة في صفقة (safqah fi safqah): One transaction within another; a prohibited combination in a single sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what happens if a buyer refuses to deliver the specified pledge?
A) The buyer is compelled to deliver the pledge.
B) The sale becomes invalid automatically.
C) The seller has the option to rescind the sale.
D) The buyer must pay a penalty.

Key Takeaway
An otherwise prohibited condition in a sale is valid by istihsan if it is suitable (mula'im) for the contract's purpose, giving the seller an option but not compulsion.

Sale Conditioned on a Specific Pawn or Guarantor: Istihsan Over Qiyas
Ruling with proof for validity of sale conditioned on specific pawn or guarantor by istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale conditioned on a specific pawn or guarantor, explain the istihsan argument, and apply the distinction between suitable and unsuitable conditions.

Core Idea
A sale conditioned on a specific pawn is valid by istihsan if the condition is suitable (mula'im) to secure the debt.

In Hanafi fiqh, the principle of istihsan often overrides strict qiyas when a condition serves the contract's purpose. This lesson examines a key case: a buyer agreeing to pawn a specific item or provide a specific guarantor, then refusing. The Hanafi school upholds the sale by istihsan, while distinguishing from the general prohibition of a 'deal within a deal'. We'll unpack the reasoning, the intra-Hanafi dispute on compulsion, and the crucial condition of specificity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sale conditioned on a specific pawn or guarantor. State the Hanafi ruling: valid (sahih) by istihsan.
The qiyas would invalidate it.
2
Understand the qiyas objection
Qiyas says the sale is invalid because it is a 'deal within a deal' (safqat fi safqa), which involves uncertainty (gharar).
This is the default ruling unless a stronger evidence overrides.
3
Analyze the istihsan argument
Istihsan overrides qiyas because the condition is suitable (mula'im): pawn and guaranty secure the debt, which aligns with the purpose of the sale.
The condition is not a separate deal; it is a means to an end.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on compulsion
Imam Abu Hanifa and the majority hold that the buyer cannot be compelled to deliver the pawn; the seller only has an option to rescind unless immediate payment or value is given. Imam Zufar argues compulsion because the pawn becomes a right of the sale.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view: no compulsion.
5
Apply the condition of specificity
The pawn or guarantor must be specific, and the guarantor must be present at the session; otherwise, the condition loses its purpose and the sale becomes invalid.
Vagueness or absence negates the benefit of security.

كتاب الرهن / تعريفه وشروطه وما يصح به والتصرف فيه
ومَن شرى شيئاً على أن يرهن شيئاً ، أو يعطي كفيلا بعينهما من ثمنه وأبي صح استحسانا
(ومن شرى شيئاً على أن يرهن شيئاً، أو يعطي كفيلاً بعينهما من ثمنه وأبى صح استحساناً، والقياس أن لا يجوز؛ لأنه صفقة في صفقة، وجه الاستحسان : أنه شرط ملائم ؛ لأنّ الكفالة والرهن للاستيثاق، والاستيثاق ملائم للوجوب ، فاعتبار وضعه لهذا المعنى يوجب إرادته خاصة به غیره، فاعتبار وضعه لهذا المعنى يوجب إرادته خاصة، واعتبار وضعه لذلك المعنى يوجب إرادته خاصة فيلزم أن تكون كل منهما مراداً، وغير مراد، فلا يكون ذلك إلا بأن يراد أحد المعنيين على أنه نفس الموضوع له، والآخر على أنه يناسبه، فيكون جمعاً بين الحقيقة والمجاز، وهو باطل.
وقال الشافعي له : يجوز ذلك بشرط أن لا يكون بينهما مضادّة، فإذا كان بينهما مضادة لا يجوز بالاتفاق، وكذا لا يجوز إرادة المجموع من حيث هو مجموع بالاتفاق.
[١] قوله : ملائم للوجوب ؛ فإذا كان الرهن معيّناً والكفيل حاضراً في المجلس اعتبرنا فيه معنى الشرط، وهو ملائم، فصح العقد، وإذا لم يكن الرهن ولا الكفيل معيناً، أو كان الكفيل غائباً حتى افترقا لم يبق معنى الكفالة، والرهن للجهالة، فبقي الاعتبار لعينه فيفسد ، ولو كان غائباً فحضر في المجلس، وقبل : صح. ولو امتنع المشتري عن تسليم الرهن لم يجبر عليه، وقال زفر: يجبر؛ لأنَّ الرهن إذا شرط في البيع صارَ حقاً من حقوقه كالوكالة المشروطة في الرهن، فيلزمه بلزومه، ونحن نقول : الرهن عقد تبرع من جانب الراهن على ما بيناه ، ولا جبر على التبرعات.
ولكن البائع بالخيار إن شاء رضي بترك الرهن، وإن شاء فسخ البيع ؛ لأنه وصف مرغوب فيه، وما رضي إلا به، فيتخيرُ بفواته إلا أن يدفع المشتري الثمن حالاً لحصول المقصود أو يدفع قيمة الرهن رهناً؛ لأنَّ يد الاستيفاء تثبت على المعنى وهو القيمة. ولا يجبر على الوفاء، وللبائع فسخه إلا إذا سَلَّمَ منه حالاً، أو قيمة الرهن رهناً وإنما قال بعينهما ؛ لأنه لو لم يكن الرهن أو الكفيل معيناً يفسد البيع.
[٢]قوله : يفسد البيع ؛ لأنهما إذا كانا مجهولين أو كان الكفيل غائباً فات معناهما، وهو الاستيفاء ؛ لأنَّ المشتري ربَّما يأتي بشيء يساوي عشراً من حقه أو يعطي كفيلاً غير غني، وليس في ذلك من التوثق، فبقي الاعتبار بعين الشرط، وهي تفسد العقد. قاله الجلبيه [٢]قوله : كالوكالة المشروطة في الرهن... الخ ؛ أي الرهن يثبت في ضمن عقد لازم وهو البيع، فيصير الوفاء به مستحقاً ، كما إذا وكل الراهن العدل أو المرتهن ببيع الرهن عند حلول الدين، فالوكاله لازمةٌ ولا يملك الراهن عزله عنها.
ولنا : إنّ الرهن عقد تبرع ، ولا جبر على المتبرع كما مر ، وإنما صار حقاً من حقوقه إذا وُجِدَ التسليم ولم يوجد بعد ؛ ولأن الرهن عقد منفرد، والعقود لا تكون بعضها من حقوق بعض قاله الجلبي.
Book of Pledge (Rahn): Its definition, conditions, what is valid, and disposition therein. And whoever buys something on condition that he will pawn something, or give a specific guarantor from its price, and then refuses, it is valid by istihsan. (And whoever buys something on condition that he will pawn something, or give a specific guarantor from its price, and then refuses, it is valid by istihsan. By qiyas it is not permissible because it is a deal within a deal. The basis of istihsan: it is a suitable condition because guaranty and pledge are for securing the debt, and securing is suitable for the obligation. So considering its placement for this meaning obligates intending it specifically to the exclusion of others. Considering its placement for that meaning obligates intending it specifically. Thus it would be that each of them is intended and not intended. That cannot be except by one of the two meanings being intended as the very thing it is placed for, and the other as suitable to it, which would be a combination of literal and metaphorical, and that is invalid.) Al-Shafi'i said: it is permissible on condition that there is no contradiction between them. If there is contradiction, it is impermissible by consensus. Likewise, intending the combination as a whole is impermissible by consensus. [1] He said: 'suitable for the obligation': when the pawn is specific and the guarantor is present in the session, we consider the meaning of the condition in it, and it is suitable, so the contract is valid. When the pawn and guarantor are not specific, or the guarantor is absent until they separate, the meaning of guaranty ceases, and the pawn is unknown, so consideration remains for its essence and it becomes invalid. If [the guarantor] was absent and then came to the session and accepted, it is valid. If the buyer refuses to deliver the pawn, he is not compelled to do so. Zufar said: he is compelled because the pawn, when stipulated in the sale, becomes a right of its rights like the agency stipulated in the pawn, so it becomes binding upon its binding. We say: the pawn is a gratuitous contract from the side of the pawnor as we explained, and there is no compulsion in gratuitous contracts. However, the seller has an option: if he wishes he may accept leaving the pawn, and if he wishes he may rescind the sale because it is a desirable description, and he only agreed with it, so he has an option upon its loss unless the buyer pays the price immediately to achieve the purpose, or gives the value of the pawn as a pledge because the hand of collection is established upon the meaning which is the value. And he is not compelled to fulfill, and the seller has the right to rescind unless he pays immediately or gives the value of the pawn as a pledge. And he only said 'specific' because if the pawn or guarantor was not specific, the sale is invalid. [2] He said: 'the sale is invalid' because when they are unknown or the guarantor is absent, their meaning is lost, which is collection; because the buyer might bring something worth a tenth of his right or give a non-wealthy guarantor, and there is no security in that, so consideration remains for the essence of the condition, which invalidates the contract. Al-Jalabi said it. [2] He said: 'like the agency stipulated in the pawn...' i.e., the pawn is established within a binding contract which is the sale, so fulfilling it becomes obligatory, as when the pawnor appoints the trustee or mortgagee to sell the pawn upon maturity of the debt, the agency becomes binding and the pawnor cannot dismiss him. Our argument: the pawn is a gratuitous contract, and there is no compulsion on the one who gives gratuitously as before, and it only becomes a right of its rights when delivery occurs, and it has not occurred yet; and because the pawn is an independent contract, and contracts are not part of the rights of each other. Al-Jalabi said it.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (istihsan vs qiyas) regarding a sale conditioned on a specific pawn or guarantor. The matn states that if a person buys something on the condition that he will pawn a specific item or give a specific guarantor from the price, and then refuses to fulfill that condition, the sale is valid by istihsan (juristic preference). The qiyas would make it invalid because it is considered a 'deal within a deal' (safqat fi safqa), which is generally prohibited in Hanafi law. However, istihsan overrides qiyas here because the condition is suitable (mula'im) to the contract: the purpose of pawn and guaranty is to secure the debt, which is suitable for the obligation of payment. The text then contrasts this with the view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who permits it only if there is no contradiction between the condition and the contract; if there is contradiction, it is invalid by consensus. The commentary clarifies that when the pawn is specific and the guarantor is present in the session, the condition is meaningful and the contract is valid; if they are unknown or the guarantor is absent until separation, the condition loses its purpose and the sale becomes invalid. A key intra-Hanafi dispute appears regarding whether the buyer can be compelled to deliver the pawn: Imam Abu Hanifa and the majority hold that he cannot be compelled because the pawn is a gratuitous contract (tabarru'), and there is no compulsion in gratuitous contracts. Imam Zufar argues that since the pawn was stipulated in the sale, it becomes a right of the sale and thus binding. The Hanafi position is that the seller has an option: he may either accept the abandonment of the pawn or rescind the sale, unless the buyer pays the price immediately or gives the value of the pawn as a pledge. The value of the pawn can serve the same purpose of security. The condition of specificity is crucial: if the pawn or guarantor is unspecified, the sale is invalid because the element of security is lost.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that abandons strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more suitable ruling due to necessity, custom, or a stronger evidence.
صفقة في صفقة (safqat fi safqa): A deal within a deal; a transaction that combines two interdependent contracts in a way that is prohibited due to uncertainty (gharar) or resembling a double sale.
ملائم (mula'im): Suitable; a condition that aligns with the purpose and nature of the contract, thus not causing harm or uncertainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone buys an item on the condition that he will pawn a specific item, and then refuses to deliver the pawn, what is the ruling?
A) The sale is invalid because it involves a deal within a deal.
B) The sale is valid by istihsan; the buyer can be compelled to deliver the pawn.
C) The sale is valid by istihsan; the buyer cannot be compelled, but the seller has an option to rescind unless the buyer pays immediately or gives the value of the pawn as a pledge.
D) The sale is valid only if the pawn is not specific; if specific, it is invalid.

Key Takeaway
A sale conditioned on a specific pawn or guarantor is valid by istihsan if the condition is suitable (mula'im) and specific; the buyer is not compelled to deliver the pawn, and the seller has an option to rescind unless immediate payment or value is given.

Seller's Right to Rescind When Pledge Condition Fails
Ruling on seller's right to rescind when pledge condition fails

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that a seller cannot be compelled to accept a pledge condition and state the seller's right to rescind, and distinguish the position of Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
A pledge condition in a sale does not bind the seller; he may rescind if the condition fails.

In a sale contract where the buyer promises to provide a pledge, what happens if the buyer fails to deliver the specific pledge? The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa, rules that the seller cannot force the buyer to provide the pledge; instead, the seller has the option to rescind the sale. Imam Zufar, however, argues that the condition becomes a binding right. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the majority Hanafi position and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal issue
The passage addresses whether a seller can be compelled to accept the fulfillment of a pledge condition stipulated in a sale contract. Determine the key question: is the condition binding or merely a desirable attribute?
The condition is that the buyer provides a specific pledge or guarantor.
2
State the majority Hanafi position and its premise
According to Abu Hanifa and the majority, the seller is not compelled to accept the condition. The reasoning is that a pledge is a voluntary contract (tabarru'), and there is no compulsion in voluntary acts. The condition gives the seller an option (khiyar) if it fails.
The condition is seen as a desirable trait, not a contractual right.
3
Analyze Imam Zufar's dissent
Imam Zufar argues that the pledge condition becomes a right of the sale, analogous to an agency condition in a pledge that becomes binding. Therefore, the seller must accept the pledge if offered later.
Zufar uses qiyas (analogy) to agency in pledge.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to Zufar
The Hanafi response refutes the analogy: the pledge is a separate contract and does not merge with the sale. Until delivery, the pledge is not binding. The condition does not transform into a right of sale.
The principle: 'Contracts are not parts of each other's rights.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under the majority view, the seller may rescind if the buyer fails to provide the pledge. Under Zufar's view, the seller must accept the pledge later. The practical difference: a rescission option vs. a binding obligation.
The majority view is the muftā bihī (operative for fatwa).

ولا يجبر على الوفاء، وللبائع فسخه إلا إذا سَلَّمَ منه حالاً ، أو قيمة الرهن رهناً وإنما قال بعينهما ؛ لأنه لو لم يكن الرهن أو الكفيل معيناً يفسد البيع، (ولا يجبر على الوفاء)، هذا عندنا ؛ لأنَّه لا جبر على التبرعات، وعند زفر ه: يجبر ؛ لأنَّ الرهن إذا شرط في البيع صارَ حقاً من حقوقه كالوكالة المشروطة في الرهن ، (وللبائع فسخه" إلا إذا سَلَّمَ ثمنه حالاً ، أو قيمة الرهن رهنا) ، إذ عندنا لما صح الشرط فإنه وصف مرغوب فيه فبفواته يكون للبائع حق الفسخ . المقصود أو يدفع قيمة الرهن رهناً ؛ لأنَّ يد الاستيفاء تثبت على المعنى وهو القيمة. كذا في «الهداية». قوله : يفسد البيع ؛ لأنهما إذا كانا مجهولين أو كان الكفيل غائباً فات معناهما، وهو الاستيفاء ؛ لأنَّ المشتري ربَّما يأتي بشيء يساوي عشراً من حقه أو يعطي كفيلاً غير غني، وليس في ذلك من التوثق، فبقي الاعتبار بعين الشرط، وهي تفسد العقد. قاله الجلبيه. قوله : كالوكالة المشروطة في الرهن... الخ ؛ أي الرهن يثبت في ضمن عقد لازم وهو البيع، فيصير الوفاء به مستحقاً ، كما إذا وكل الراهن العدل أو المرتهن ببيع الرهن عند حلول الدين، فالوكاله لازمةٌ ولا يملك الراهن عزله عنها. ولنا : إنّ الرهن عقد تبرع ، ولا جبر على المتبرع كما مر ، وإنما صار حقاً من حقوقه إذا وُجِدَ التسليم ولم يوجد بعد ؛ ولأن الرهن عقد منفرد، والعقود لا تكون بعضها من حقوق بعض قاله الجلبي. قوله : وللبائع فسخه ...الخ ؛ أي إن للبائع الخيار إن شاء رضي بترك الدين، وإن شاء فسخ البيع ؛ لأنه وصف مرغوب فيه ؛ لفواته يوجب الخيار ؛ كسلامة المبيع عن العيب في البيع إلا أن يدفع المشتري الثمن حالاً ؛ لحصول المقصود أو يدفع قيمة الرهن رهناً ؛ لأنَّ المقصود من الرهن المشروط يحصل بقيمته.
And he is not compelled to fulfill (the pledge), and the seller has the right to rescind it, except if he pays the price immediately, or (pays) the value of the pledge as a pledge. And (the author) only said "by their specification" because if the pledge or the guarantor were unspecified, the sale would be invalid. (He is not compelled to fulfill) — this is according to us, because there is no compulsion on voluntary acts. And according to Zufar: he is compelled, because when the pledge is stipulated in the sale, it becomes a right from its rights, like the agency stipulated in the pledge. (And the seller has the right to rescind it) except if he pays the price immediately, or the value of the pledge as a pledge — because according to us, when the condition is valid, it is a desirable attribute, so with its failure, the seller has the right of rescission. The purpose is that he pays the value of the pledge as a pledge, because the hand of recovery is established upon the meaning, which is the value. Thus in al-Hidayah. He said: the sale is invalid because if they are unknown or the guarantor is absent, their meaning is lost, which is recovery; because the buyer may bring something worth a tenth of his right or give a non-wealthy guarantor, and there is no securing in that, so consideration remains upon the condition itself, and it invalidates the contract. Said by al-Jalabi. He said: like the agency stipulated in the pledge... i.e., the pledge is established within a binding contract, which is the sale, so fulfillment becomes obligatory, as when the pledgor authorizes the trustee or the mortgagee to sell the pledge at the maturity of the debt, the agency is binding and the pledgor cannot dismiss it. Our argument: The pledge is a voluntary contract, and there is no compulsion on the volunteer, as previously; and it becomes a right from its rights only when delivery exists, and it has not yet occurred; and because the pledge is a separate contract, and contracts are not parts of each other's rights. Said by al-Jalabi. He said: And the seller has the right to rescind it... i.e., the seller has the option: if he wishes, he is content with leaving the debt, and if he wishes, he rescinds the sale, because it is a desirable attribute; its failure necessitates an option, like the soundness of the sold item from a defect in sale, unless the buyer pays the price immediately, for the attainment of the purpose, or pays the value of the pledge as a pledge, because the purpose of the stipulated pledge is attained by its value.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with an intra-Hanafi dispute. The text begins by stating the ruling: the seller is not compelled to accept the buyer's fulfillment of a pledge condition stipulated in the sale. If the buyer fails to provide the specified pledge or guarantor, or the specified item is unknown, the sale is invalid. However, if the condition is valid but unfulfilled, the seller has the right to rescind the sale unless the buyer pays the price immediately or offers the value of the pledge as a substitute pledge. The author then clarifies that this is the position of Abu Hanifa (referred to as 'us'), because a pledge is a voluntary contract (tabarru'), and no one can be compelled to perform a voluntary act. Imam Zufar disagrees, arguing that the pledge condition becomes a right of the sale contract, analogous to an agency condition in a pledge, which becomes binding. The Hanafi response rejects this analogy: the pledge is a separate contract, and until delivery, it does not become a right of the sale. The commentary further explains that the purpose of the pledge is to secure payment, and that can be achieved by paying the price or the pledge's value. The ruling is from the relied-upon view (muftā bihī) of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A pledge; a contract where property is held as security for a debt.
جبر (jabr): Compulsion; forcing someone to perform an act.
تبرع (tabarru'): A voluntary act or contract without direct exchange.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a buyer fails to provide the specified pledge item as stipulated in a sale contract?
A) The seller can force the buyer to provide the pledge.
B) The seller has the right to rescind the sale.
C) The sale becomes void automatically.
D) The buyer must pay the price immediately regardless.

Key Takeaway
In a sale, a pledge condition is a desirable attribute, not a binding right; the seller may rescind if it fails, but cannot compel its performance.
